1e0e9 LVINLBVWd
1e0fb 6Selects the GPIB bus on which to perform the operation.  The VI addresses the interface indicated by bus as a Listener.  If you have only one GPIB interface in your computer, the default bus number is 0. For additional GPIB interfaces, see the software installation instructions included with your GPIB board.
1e236 Termination mode specifies how the GPIB driver should determine when the read is finished.  All values from 0-255 (0x0-0xFF) will be taken to be an eos byte which wll stop the read when it is recieved in the data stream or when end is detected.  STOPend 256 (0x100) (the default) indicates to stop the read when end is detected.  The read  will always stop when the requested count has been read.
1e3c6 status is a Boolean array in which each bit describes a state of the GPIB Controller. If an error occurs, the GPIB VIs set bit 15. GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
1e47e GPIB status vector:
1e493 status[0] - Device Clear State
1e4b2  status[1] - Device Trigger State
1e4d4  status[2] - Listener Active State
1e4f8 status[3] - Talker Active State
1e519 status[4] - Attention line asserted
1e53e status[5] -
1e54a Controller In Charge
1e55f  status[6] - Remote State
1e579  status[7] - Lockout State
1e595 status[8] - I/O Completed 
1e5b1 status[9] - not used
1e5c6  status[10]- not used
1e5dc  status[11]- not used
1e5f3 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
1e61b status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
1e63b  status[14]- Timeout occured
1e658  status[15]- GPIB error detected
1e67c GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
1e6b1 GPIB Error:
1e6c2 -No error
1e6d1 -Function requires GPIB to be CIC
1e6f8 -No listeners detected on write
1e71d -Controller not addressed correctly
1e746 -Invalid argument(s)
1e761 (perhaps bad address string????)
1e787 -Function requires GPIB to be SC
1e7ad -I/O operation aborted
1e7c9 -hardware not present
1e7e4 -DMA error
1e7f4 -DMA bus timeout
1e80a -New I/O attempted while I/O in 
1e831 progress
1e83f -function not implemented
1e85e -file system error
1e876 -shareable board exclusively owned
1e89e -GPIB bus error (commands)
1e8be -Serial Poll Byte Lost
1e8da -SRQ line cannot be cleared
1e8fb -Unrecognized commandEAbyte count refers to the number of bytes that pass over the GPIB.
1e955 This integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  Use MakeAddress.vi to construct a GPIB address which uses secondary addressing.RNcount. The VI returns up to count data bytes from the device in data string. 
1eaa3 GPIB status vector:
1eab8 status[0] - Device Clear State
1ead7  status[1] - Device Trigger State
1eaf9  status[2] - Listener Active State
1eb1d status[3] - Talker Active State
1eb3e status[4] - Attention line asserted
1eb63 status[5] -
1eb6f Controller In Charge
1eb84  status[6] - Remote State
1eb9e  status[7] - Lockout State
1ebba status[8] - I/O Completed 
1ebd6 status[9] - not used
1ebeb  status[10]- not used
1ec01  status[11]- not used
1ec18 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
1ec40 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
1ec60  status[14]- Timeout occured
1ec7d  status[15]- GPIB error detectedA=data string contains count data bytes from the GPIB device.

2c8c5 GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set. 
2c8fb GPIB Error:
2c90c -No error
2c91b -Function requires GPIB to be CIC
2c942 -No listeners detected on write
2c967 -Controller not addressed correctly
2c990 -Invalid argument(s)
2c9ab (perhaps bad address string????)
2c9d1 -Function requires GPIB to be SC
2c9f7 -I/O operation aborted
2ca13 -hardware not present
2ca2e -DMA error
2ca3e -DMA bus timeout
2ca54 -New I/O attempted while I/O in 
2ca7b progress
2ca89 -function not implemented
2caa8 -file system error
2cac0 -shareable board exclusively owned
2cae8 -GPIB bus error (commands)
2cb08 -Serial Poll Byte Lost
2cb24 -SRQ line cannot be cleared
2cb45 -Unrecognized commandEAbyte count refers to the number of bytes that pass over the GPIB.
2cba1 status is a Boolean array in which each bit describes a state of the GPIB Controller. If an error occurs, the GPIB VIs set bit 15. GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
2cc59 GPIB status vector:
2cc6e status[0] - Device Clear State
2cc8d  status[1] - Device Trigger State
2ccaf  status[2] - Listener Active State
2ccd3 status[3] - Talker Active State
2ccf4 status[4] - Attention line asserted
2cd19 status[5] -
2cd25 Controller In Charge
2cd3a  status[6] - Remote State
2cd54  status[7] - Lockout State
2cd70 status[8] - I/O Completed 
2cd8c status[9] - not used
2cda1  status[10]- not used
2cdb7  status[11]- not used
2cdce status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
2cdf6 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
2ce16  status[14]- Timeout occured
2ce33  status[15]- GPIB error detected
2ce55 This integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  Use MakeAddress.vi to construct a GPIB address which uses secondary addressing.
2cf52 3Selects the GPIB bus on which to perform the operation.  The VI addresses the interface indicated by bus as a Talker. If you have only one GPIB interface in your computer, the default bus number is 0. For additional GPIB interfaces, see the software installation instructions included with your GPIB board.
2d088 The end of transfer mode describes the method of signaling the end of the data to the listener.  Its values are:
2d0f9   2 (default) DABend - Send eoi with last byte.
2d129  1 NL end - Send linefeed with eoi after data.
2d158  0 NULLend - Do nothing at end of transfer.OKdata string contains the data bytes that the VI sends to the GPIB device.

2d1e9 status[0] - Device Clear State
2d208  status[1] - Device Trigger State
2d22a  status[2] - Listener Active State
2d24e status[3] - Talker Active State
2d26f status[4] - Attention line asserted
2d294 status[5] -
2d2a0 Controller In Charge

2d2cf  status[7] - Lockout State

2d307 status[9] - not used

2d332  status[11]- not used
2d349 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC

6acc0 LVINLBVWgH
6acd2 /Primary GPIB address ranging from 0 to 30.  Used to form the low order byte of the GPIB address which will be accepted by 488.2 functions.  The value of 31 (default) means return the NOADDR constant (0xFFFF) as the packed address.  The VI places primary address in the lower byte of the packed address.
6ae06 Secondary GPIB address ranging from 0 to 30.  Used to form the high order byte of the GPIB address which will be accepted by 488.2 functions. The value of 31 (default) means use no secondary address. The VI places secondary address in the upper byte of the packed address.
6af1a VThis integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  packed address contains primary address in its lower byte and secondary address in its upper byte. You can use packed address as the address input to the GPIB 488.2 VIs. 
6b073 True if either primary or secondary addresses are outside ot the range 0-31.  address error indicates whether a range error has occurred.

75cc1 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
75dbd (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
75f16      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
75f4a      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
75f84      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
75fbd      error, and a positive value is a warning.
75fed      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
7601f      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.

9ac5b A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
9ad57 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
9aeb0      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
9aee4      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
9af1e      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
9af57      error, and a positive value is a warning.
9af87      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
9afb9      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
9afea [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred."

9b152 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters:

b58e3 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
b5a3c      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
b5a70      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
b5aaa      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
b5ae3      error, and a positive value is a warning.
b5b13      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
b5b45      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
b5b76 [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
b5c02 (ABC) Uniquely identifies the instrument to establish communications with.  The grammar for the instrument descriptor is shown below.  Parameters are shown in lower-case and optional parameters are shown in square brackets ([]).
b5ce8 GPIB:   INSTR{GPIB[bd]::prim addr[::sec addr]}
b5d17 VXI:  INSTR{VXI::logical addr}
b5d36 GPIB-VXI:   INSTR{GPIB-VXI[bd]::logical addr[prim addr]}
b5d70 Optional Parameter Default Values:
b5d93     bd - GPIB board (0)
b5dab     prim addr - GPIB primary address (1)
b5dd4     sec addr - GPIB secondary address (none)
b5e01     logical addr - VXI logical address 
b5e2a EXAMPLE:  A GPIB instrument on GPIB board 0, at primary address 5, and no secondary addressing.
b5e8c INSTR{GPIB::5}"
b5e9d no error
b5ea6 ERROR
b5eac no error
b5eb5 ERROR
b5ebc (ABC) 
b5ec3 The name of the VI that is calling this VI.  If an error occurs during the operation of this VI, the value in source will be placed in the source element of the error out cluster. 
b5f7a (I32) 
b5f81 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
b607c f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
b617e      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
b61b1      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
b61e0      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
b621a      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
b6253      error, and a positive value is a warning.
b6283      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
b62b2      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
b62e3 ZV(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing."

b634d no error
b6356 ERROR
b635d (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.  A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an error, and a positive value is a warning.[W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
b644d (i32) The error code associated with an error.  Possible values:
b648f 0  Success
b649a -1200  Invalid syntax string
b64b7 -1201  Error finding instruments
b64d8 -1202  Unable to initialize interface or instrument
b650c -1205  Invalid instr handle
b6528 -1210  Parameter out of range
b6546 -1220  Error getting attribute
b6565 -1221  Error setting attribute
b6584 -1224  Error clearing instrument
b65a5 -1225  Error triggering instrument
b65c8 -1226  Error polling instrument
b65e8 -1230  Error writing to instrument
b660b -1231  Error reading from instrument
b6630 -1240  Instrument timed out
b664c -1250  Error mapping VXI address
b666d -1251  Error unmapping VXI address
b6690 -1252  Error accessing VXIbus
b66ae -1260  Function not supported by controller

d57d4 pattern
d57df iteration (0:initialize)
d5807 Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
d58ba The Read from Digital Port VI reads a user configured digital port.  The reading is displayed as a binary number in [pattern].
d593a You have the option to not reconfigure the port as an input port by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value. You can also concatenate multiple ports to operate as one large port by using the port width paramter.
d5a19 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8.
d5aa0 Please read the DAQ VI Reference Manual for descriptions of Digital Port Configure and Digital Port Read for more information.yudevice is the device number you assigned to the plug-in DAQ board during configuration. This parameter defaults to 1.
d5b98 =port width is the total width in bits or the number of lines of the port. For example, you can combine two 4bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8. 
d5c4f When port width is greater than the physical width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5. 
d5dd8 (U32) pattern: contains the binary data read from the port. Bit zero is the least significant bit from the port specified by the port number control. 
d5e71 J(i32) iteration: controls when the VI performs initialization.  If iteration is 0, the VI configures the port for input and then reads the data.  If iteration is greater than zero, the VI assumes that configuration has already been done and simply reads the data.  You usually wire this input from a While loop iteration terminal.
d5fbf )port number specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use a digital SCXI module, use the SCx!MDy!0 syntax, where x is the chassis ID and y is the module device number, to specify the port on a module.

dc41e iteration (0:initialize)
dc446 Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
dc4f9 The Write to Digital Port VI outputs a pattern (in binary) to a specified digital port.  
dc554 You can control the number of lines in a port by the parameter port width.  You also have the option of not reconfiguring the port as an output port with each iteration of the VI by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value.
dc63e Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8. 
dc6c6 Please read the DAQ VI Reference Manual for descriptions of Digital Port Configure and Digital Port Write for more information.yudevice is the device number you assigned to the plug-in DAQ board during configuration. This parameter defaults to 1.
dc7bf &port width is the total width in bits of the port. For example, you can combine two 4bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8. 
dc85f When port width is greater than the physical width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5. 
dc9e8 (U32) pattern: contains the binary data to write to the port. Bit zero is the least significant bit for the port specified by the port number control. 
dca82 M(i32) iteration: controls when the VI performs initialization.  If iteration is 0, the VI configures the port for output and then writes the data.  If iteration is greater than zero, the VI assumes that configuration has already been done and simply writes the data.  You usually wire this input from a While loop iteration terminal.
dcbd3 )port number specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use a digital SCXI module, use the SCx!MDy!0 syntax, where x is the chassis ID and y is the module device number, to specify the port on a module.

f5fa7  INSTRUCTIONS:
f5fb7 Normal Use:  When using subVIs that incorporate the error in/error out (or error I/O) structure, place this handler where you want to inform the user of an error, typically at the end of the I/O data path, as the last action of the program.  If the error in status is ERROR, the handler creates a message describing the error and its source.  If the type of dialog = 1 (default), the message is displayed to the user, who can only acknowedge it.  If the type = 2, the user can acknowledge the message or abort execution; aborting a program with active I/O is not recommended.  If the type = 0, no message is displayed; this is used to process the error programmatically, and the error out cluster elements are wired to individual terminals for that reason.  
f62af Other Uses:
f62bd local testing.  To test the error code of a subVI or function that does not have the error I/O structure, you can wire its error code and a source string to the local error code and error source inputs.  If error in status indicates no error and error code is not equal to 0, the local code and source are substituted for the error in values, and the status is set TRUE (ERROR).
f6439 user-defined codes.  The error handler has tables of error codes and descriptions for all LabVIEW I/O operations (file, GPIB, DAQ, etc.).  You can augment the tables with the user-defined arrays.  Codes from 5000 to 9999 are reserved for user assignments.
f653a exception handling.  This mechanism is available either to set the error out status FALSE on what is normally an error or to set the status TRUE on what is normally not an error.  If exception action > 0, the error in code and source are checked.  If they match the exception code and source, the error out status is adjusted accordingly.  That is, if the action = 1, the error out status is set to FALSE and code is set to zero and if the action = 2, the error out is set to TRUE and the code is unchanged.  An empty exception source matches any error in source.  
f6778 . Interpret it bit-wise as follows: x4000: serial port VI error; x0001: receiving queue overflowed or character was received after end-of-file character; x0002: character was lost by overwrite; x0004: parity error; x0008: framing error; x0010: break condition; x0020: CTS timeout; x0040:  DSR timeout; x0080: RLSD timeout; x0100: transmission queue was full when new character arrived; x0200: parallel device timeout; x0400: parallel device I/O error; x0800: parallel device not selected; x1000: parallel device out of paper; x8000: requested mode is  not supported or the idComDev parameter is invalid.  Consult the LabVIEW serial port manual for more information.

f6fa1 message
f6fb0 GetCommErr"
f6fd0 1This error handler is used primarily to inform the user if an input error exists, to describe the error, and to identify where it occurred.  The information for this is derived from the inputs error in, error code, and error source, and from an internal error description table.  The table describes all errors that can be created by LabVIEW or its associated I/O operations.  The handler has provisions to take alternative actions, such as to cancel or set an error status, and to test for and describe user-defined errors.  See instruction on the front panel.
f7205 =type of dialog determines what type dialog box will be displayed, if any. Regardless of its value, the VI outputs error information and message describing the error.
f72b0 displays no dialog box. This is useful if you want to have programmatic control over how the error is handled.
f7323 (the default value) displays a dialog box with a single OK button. After the user responds, the VI returns control to the main VI.
f73aa displays a dialog box with buttons allowing the user to either continue or stop. If the user cancels, the VI calls the Stop function to halt execution. 
f7443 HDcode out is the error code indicated by the error in or error code.
f7489 b^exception code is the error code that you want to treat as an exception. By default, it is 0.
f74eb error code is a numeric error code. If error in indicates an error, the VI ignores error code. If not, the VI tests it. A non-zero value signifies an error.
f758a user-defined codes is an array of the numeric error codes you define in your VIs. The VI searches this array after searching the internal list of error codes. Codes in the range of 5000 to 9999 are reserved for users.
f7666 user-defined descriptions is an array of descriptions of user-defined codes. If an incoming error matches one in user-defined codes, the VI uses the corresponding description from user-defined descriptions in message.
f7740 2.source out indicates the source of the error.
f7770 }yexception source is the error message that you want to use to test for an exception. By default, it is an empty string. 
f77ed error source is an optional string you can use to describe the source of error code. The VI uses the string in message if there is an error.
f787e exception action is a way for you to create exceptions to error handling. You can treat what is normally an error as no error, or treat a no error condition as an error using this parameter. 
f7942 (the default value) performs no error exception handling. 
f7981 cancels error under the following conditions:
f79b1 If the VI detects an error, as described in the status and error code parameters, and if that error code value matches exception code and the error source value matches exception source, the VI sets status out to FALSE, code out to 0, and source out to an empty string. An empty exception source string matches any error source string.
f7b05 sets error under the following conditions:
f7b32 If the VI detects no error, as described in the status and error code parameters, but the code value of error in matches exception code and the error source value matches exception source, the VI sets status out to TRUE, code out to the code value from error in, and source out to the source value from error in.
f7c6b jferror in describes an error that you want to check. If unwired, this VI checks error code for errors.
f7cd5 status is TRUE if an error occurred. If this value is FALSE, then the error handler assumes that no error occurred according to the error in, and then checks the error code.
f7d83 51code is the error code associated with an error.
f7db8 source. In case of an error, most VIs that use the error in and error out clusters set source to the name of the VI or function that produced the error.
f7e51 |xerror out contains the same information as status out, code out, and source out. It has the same structure as error in.
f7ecd status is TRUE if an error occurred. If this value is FALSE, then the error handler assumes that no error occurred according to the error in, and then checks the error code.
f7f7b 51code is the error code associated with an error.
f7fb0 source. In case of an error, most VIs that use the error in and error out clusters set source to the name of the VI or function that produced the error.
f8049 mimessage describes the error code that occurred, the source of the error, and a description of the error.

f8bdf GetCommErr
f8c02 . Interpret it bit-wise as follows: x4000: serial port VI error; x0001: receiving queue overflowed or character was received after end-of-file character; x0002: character was lost by overwrite; x0004: parity error; x0008: framing error; x0010: break condition; x0020: CTS timeout; x0040:  DSR timeout; x0080: RLSD timeout; x0100: transmission queue was full when new character arrived; x0200: parallel device timeout; x0400: parallel device I/O error; x0800: parallel device not selected; x1000: parallel device out of paper; x8000: requested mode is  not supported or the idComDev parameter is invalid.  Consult the LabVIEW serial port manual for more information.SD
f8eae message
f8f29  INSTRUCTIONS:
f8f39 Normal Use:  When using subVIs that incorporate the error in/error out (or error I/O) structure, place this handler where you want to inform the user of an error, typically at the end of the I/O data path, as the last action of the program.  If the error in status is ERROR, the handler creates a message describing the error and its source.  If the type of dialog = 1 (default), the message is displayed to the user, who can only acknowedge it.  If the type = 2, the user can acknowledge the message or abort execution; aborting a program with active I/O is not recommended.  If the type = 0, no message is displayed; this is used to process the error programmatically, and the error out cluster elements are wired to individual terminals for that reason.  
f9231 Other Uses:
f923f local testing.  To test the error code of a subVI or function that does not have the error I/O structure, you can wire its error code and a source string to the local error code and error source inputs.  If error in status indicates no error and error code is not equal to 0, the local code and source are substituted for the error in values, and the status is set TRUE (ERROR).
f93bb user-defined codes.  The error handler has tables of error codes and descriptions for all LabVIEW I/O operations (file, GPIB, DAQ, etc.).  You can augment the tables with the user-defined arrays.  Codes from 5000 to 9999 are reserved for user assignments.
f94bc exception handling.  This mechanism is available either to set the error out status FALSE on what is normally an error or to set the status TRUE on what is normally not an error.  If exception action > 0, the error in code and source are checked.  If they match the exception code and source, the error out status is adjusted accordingly.  That is, if the action = 1, the error out status is set to FALSE and code is set to zero and if the action = 2, the error out is set to TRUE and the code is unchanged.  An empty exception source matches any error in source.  H

105d68 For most applications, you only need to connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.
105dd1 This VI establishes a port configuration. You can use the task ID that this VI returns only in digital port VIs.
105e43 See the Data Acquisition VI Reference Manual for your platform for tables listing the default settings and ranges for this VI for the boards with which it will work.gc(i16) device: the device number you assigned to the data acquisition device when you configured it.
105f50 /(i16) port width: the total width in bits of the port. For example, you can combine two 4-bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8.
105ff5 When port width is greater than the physical port width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port  number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5.
106183 ?(i32) line direction map: specifies the direction of each line in the port. If a bit is 0 in the line map, the line is an input line. If a bit is 1, the line is an output line. Setting line direction map to -1 makes all the lines in a port output lines. Setting line direction map to 0 makes all the lines in a port input lines. Except for the NB-TIO-10 and PC-TIO-10, this is how you must use line direction map. The NB-TIO-10 and PC-TIO-10 are the only boards on which you can configure lines within a port for different directions. The default for line direction map is 0.
1063c5 (u32) task ID: uniquely identifies the group. You use this value as the task ID to refer to this group in subsequent digital port VI calls.
106454 (cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
10651c      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
106550      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
10658a      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an 
1065c4      error, and a positive value is a warning.
1065f4      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
106626      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
106657 xt(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. Regardless of the value of status, this VI clears the input operation.
1066d0 D(string) port number: specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use an SCXI-1160, SCXI-1161, SCXI-1162, or SCXI-1163 module, use the SCx!MDy syntax, where x is the chassis and y is the module device number, to specify the module.
106817 (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.  A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an error, and a positive value is a warning.[W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
106907 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
106a60      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
106a94      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
106ace      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an 
106b08      error, and a positive value is a warning.

10da34 ZFor most applications, you only need to connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.
10da9e This VI reads the port identified by task ID and returns the pattern read.
10daea See the Data Acquisition VI Reference Manual for your platform for tables listing the default settings and ranges for this VI for the boards with which it will work.
10db93 (i32) line mask: determines which lines this VI reads. If you set line mask to -1 (all ones), the VI reads the entire port. If you set only bit n in line mask, the VI reads only line n of the port. If the state of line n is high, the VI sets bit n of pattern. The VI sets to 0 the bits of pattern that correspond to lines the VI has not read. The default setting for line mask is -1 which is shown as all ones since the binary representation is the default selection.62(u32) pattern: the data the VI read from the port.51(u32) task ID out: has the same value as task ID.

114b22 VFor most applications, you only need to connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.
114b8c This VI writes the value in pattern to the port identified by task ID.
114bd4 See the Data Acquisition VI Reference Manual for your platform for tables listing the default settings and ranges for this VI for the boards with which it will work.84(u32) task ID: identifies the group and I/O pattern.D@(u32) pattern: specifies the new state of the lines in the port.
114cf4 x(i32) line mask: determines which lines in the port the write affects. If you set line mask to -1, the VI writes to the entire port and sets all the lines in the port to the states specified by the bits in pattern. If you set only bit n in line mask, the VI changes only line n in the port to the state that bit n of pattern specifies. The default setting for line mask is -1.51(u32) task ID out: has the same value as task ID.
114ea4 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
114ffd      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
115031      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
11506b      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an 
1150a5      error, and a positive value is a warning.
1150d5      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
115107      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
115138 1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
115169 (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.  A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an error, and a positive value is a warning.[W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.xt(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. Regardless of the value of status, this VI clears the input operation.
1152cf (cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
115397      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
1153cb      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
115405      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an 
11543f      error, and a positive value is a warning.
11546f      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
1154a1      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
1154d4 (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.  A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an error, and a positive value is a warning.[W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.

14e672 Write & Read
14e680 Write Only
14e68b Read Only
14e695 Mode
14e6a7 This vi performs general purpose RS-232 communication.
14e6de Timeout: (value in seconds)
14e6fa Mode:
14e700 0 = write then read, 1 = write only, 2 = read only
14e733 Port Select:
14e740 0 = com1, 1 = com2
14e755 |error in is a cluster that describes the error status before this VI executes. If error in indicates that an error occurred before this VI was called, this VI may choose not to execute its function, but just pass the error through to its error out cluster. If no error has occurred, then this VI executes normally and sets its own error status in error out. Use the error handler VIs to look up the error code and to display the corresponding error message. Using error in and error out clusters is a convenient way to check errors and to specify execution order by wiring the error output from one subVI to the error input of the next.
14e9d4 status is TRUE if an error occurred before this VI was called, or FALSE if not. If status is TRUE, code is a non-zero error code. If status is FALSE, code can be zero or a warning code.
14ea91 code is the number identifying an error or warning. If status is TRUE, code is a non-zero error code. If status is FALSE, code can be zero or a warning code. Use the error handler VIs to look up the meaning of this code and to display the corresponding error message.
14eb9e source is a string that indicates the origin of the error, if any. Usually source is the name of the VI in which the error occurred.
14ec25 error out is a cluster that describes the error status after this VI executes. If an error occurred before this VI was called, error out is the same as error in. Otherwise, error out shows the error, if any, that occurred in this VI. Use the error handler VIs to look up the error code and to display the corresponding error message. Using error in and error out clusters is a convenient way to check errors and to specify execution order by wiring the error output from one subVI to the error input of the next.
14ee27 status is TRUE if an error occurred, or FALSE if not. If status is TRUE, code is a non-zero error code. If status is FALSE, code can be zero or a warning code.
14eeca code is the number identifying an error or warning. If status is TRUE, code is a non-zero error code. If status is FALSE, code can be zero or a warning code. Use the error handler VIs to look up the meaning of this code and to display the corresponding error message.
14efd7 source is a string that indicates the origin of the error, if any. Usually source is the name of the VI in which the error occurred.

158779 error out is a cluster that describes the error status after this VI executes. If an error occurred before this VI was called, error out is the same as error in. Otherwise, error out shows the error, if any, that occurred in this VI. Use the error handler VIs to look up the error code and to display the corresponding error message. Using error in and error out clusters is a convenient way to check errors and to specify execution order by wiring the error output from one subVI to the error input of the next.
15897b status is TRUE if an error occurred, or FALSE if not. If status is TRUE, code is a non-zero error code. If status is FALSE, code can be zero or a warning code.
158a1e code is the number identifying an error or warning. If status is TRUE, code is a non-zero error code. If status is FALSE, code can be zero or a warning code. Use the error handler VIs to look up the meaning of this code and to display the corresponding error message.
158b2b source is a string that indicates the origin of the error, if any. Usually source is the name of the VI in which the error occurred."

1851ce RD8840A.VI
1851e0 This VI loads the addressing information about the instrument into the Open VXI Instrument VI and returns the instrument ID.  You can reset the instrument by setting the front panel reset control.  You must run this VI before using any of the instrument driver VIs for this instrument.
185308 Computes the mean value and the standard deviation (STD) of the values in the input sequence X. The mean and standard deviation are computed using the following formulas:
1853b4       mean = Sum { X[i] } / n.
1853d4       STD = sqrt( Sum{ (X[i] - mean)^2 } / n ).
18540b QWrites the data in string to write to the serial port indicated in port number. 
185467 qReads the number of characters specified by requested byte count from the serial port indicated in port number. 
1854e3 kReturns in byte count the number of bytes in the input buffer of the serial port indicated in port number.
185558 This vi performs general purpose RS-232 communication.
18558f Timeout: (value in seconds)
1855ab Mode:
1855b1 0 = write then read, 1 = write only, 2 = read only
1855e4 Port Select:
1855f1 0 = com1, 1 = com2
18560c This vi handles the RS-232 communications for a UUT. FC In and FC Out are used for flow control.
18566d Mode 0 - Write then Read.
185687 Mode 1 - Write only.
18569c Mode 2 - Read only.
1856b0 Timeout is in seconds.
1856cf VFor most applications, you only need to connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.
185739 This VI writes the value in pattern to the port identified by task ID.
185781 See the Data Acquisition VI Reference Manual for your platform for tables listing the default settings and ranges for this VI for the boards with which it will work.
18582f ZFor most applications, you only need to connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.
185899 This VI reads the port identified by task ID and returns the pattern read.
1858e5 See the Data Acquisition VI Reference Manual for your platform for tables listing the default settings and ranges for this VI for the boards with which it will work.
185994 For most applications, you only need to connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.
1859fd This VI establishes a port configuration. You can use the task ID that this VI returns only in digital port VIs.
185a6f See the Data Acquisition VI Reference Manual for your platform for tables listing the default settings and ranges for this VI for the boards with which it will work.
185b1b 1This error handler is used primarily to inform the user if an input error exists, to describe the error, and to identify where it occurred.  The information for this is derived from the inputs error in, error code, and error source, and from an internal error description table.  The table describes all errors that can be created by LabVIEW or its associated I/O operations.  The handler has provisions to take alternative actions, such as to cancel or set an error status, and to test for and describe user-defined errors.  See instruction on the front panel.
185d58 Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
185e0b The Write to Digital Port VI outputs a pattern (in binary) to a specified digital port.  
185e66 You can control the number of lines in a port by the parameter port width.  You also have the option of not reconfiguring the port as an output port with each iteration of the VI by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value.
185f50 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8. 
185fd8 Please read the DAQ VI Reference Manual for descriptions of Digital Port Configure and Digital Port Write for more information.
186060 Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
186113 The Read from Digital Port VI reads a user configured digital port.  The reading is displayed as a binary number in [pattern].
186193 You have the option to not reconfigure the port as an input port by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value. You can also concatenate multiple ports to operate as one large port by using the port width paramter.
186272 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8.
1862f9 Please read the DAQ VI Reference Manual for descriptions of Digital Port Configure and Digital Port Read for more information.
18637f 5Generalized DIO96 control.
18639c Device:  Card ID.
1863ae Port Number: (0-11); APA=0, APB=1,APC=2,BPA=3,...
1863e0 Port Width: Width of port in # of bits.
186408 Initialize: If zero, port will be initialized.
186437 Input: Data, if any, to be written to the port.
186467 Read/Write: Bool., F=Read, T=Write.
18648b Output: Data written to or read from port.

189270 VISA session (for class)
189291 This VI loads the addressing information about the instrument into the Open VXI Instrument VI and returns the instrument ID.  You can reset the instrument by setting the front panel reset control.  You must run this VI before using any of the instrument driver VIs for this instrument.
1893b1 (I32) 
1893b8 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
1894b3 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
1895b5      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
1895e8      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
189617      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
189651      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
18968a      error, and a positive value is a warning.
1896ba      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
1896e9      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
18971c The status boolean is either TRUE (X) for an error, or FALSE (checkmark) for no error or a warning.
189781 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
1897e9 The code input identifies the error or warning.
18981a The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
189882 The source string describes the origin of the error or warning.
1898c3 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
18992d (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
189a86      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
189aba      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
189af4      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
189b2d      error, and a positive value is a warning.
189b5d      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
189b8f      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
189bc2 The status boolean is either TRUE (X) for an error, or FALSE (checkmark) for no error or a warning.
189c27 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
189c8f The source string describes the origin of the error or warning.
189cd0 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
189d38 The code input identifies the error or warning.
189d69 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

191d5b (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
191eb4      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
191ee8      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
191f22      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
191f5b      error, and a positive value is a warning.
191f8b      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
191fbd      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
191ff0 The status boolean is either TRUE (X) for an error, or FALSE (checkmark) for no error or a warning.
192055 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
